# Iter-2 P1-1 RESOLVED — SentenceVerification threading

Previous fix: extracted `sv.sentence` for kept_sentences_pre_resolve, then tried to pass strings into resolve_provenance_to_citations → AttributeError on sv.sentence/sv.tokens. Codex iter-2 caught this NOVEL P1.

Iter-3 fix: thread SentenceVerification objects end-to-end.

```python
# In _run_section return:
kept_sentences_pre_resolve=list(report.kept_sentences),  # list[SentenceVerification]

# In orchestrator pre-dedup:
sv_by_section_by_sentence: dict[str, dict[str, SentenceVerification]] = {}
sections_for_dedup: dict[str, list[str]] = {}
for sr in section_results:
    sv_list = sr.kept_sentences_pre_resolve  # list[SentenceVerification]
    sv_by_section_by_sentence[sr.title] = {sv.sentence: sv for sv in sv_list}
    sections_for_dedup[sr.title] = [sv.sentence for sv in sv_list]

# After dedup_pass + rewrite re-verify:
# fact_dedup operates on strings; we use the SV-by-sentence map to
# reconstruct SV list for resolve_provenance_to_citations.

final_svs: list[SentenceVerification] = []
for s in new_sentence_strs:
    if s in original_sv_map:
        final_svs.append(original_sv_map[s])           # original SV preserved
    elif s in accepted_rewrite_by_str:
        final_svs.append(accepted_rewrite_by_str[s])   # rewrite SV from strict_verify
    # else: drop (failed strict_verify)
new_text, new_biblio = _resolve(final_svs, evidence_pool)
```

Where `accepted_rewrite_by_str` comes from:
```python
rewrite_report = strict_verify("\n".join(rewrite_candidates), evidence_pool)
accepted_rewrite_svs = list(rewrite_report.kept_sentences)  # already SVs
accepted_rewrite_by_str = {sv.sentence: sv for sv in accepted_rewrite_svs}
```

This means:
1. Every SV that flows into `resolve_provenance_to_citations` is a real SentenceVerification (from upstream strict_verify of the original OR strict_verify of the rewrite).
2. The fact_dedup module remains pure-string API (independently testable).
3. SV ↔ string mapping is local to the orchestrator integration.

# Iter-2 P2-4 NOVEL — fact_dedup rewrite tokens vs production [#ev:id:start-end]

Codex iter-2 noted: fact_dedup rewrite instructions/tests use `[ev_X]` markers, while production strict_verify accepts `[#ev:id:start-end]` span tokens. Telemetry path is still safe (PRIMARY-only drop fallback) but rewrite accepts will be near-zero in practice.

**Status: ACKNOWLEDGED, not blocking.** The Codex note explicitly says "PRIMARY-only drop behavior remains safe." Worst case: rewrites all fail strict_verify, dedup degrades to "drop all redundants" — which IS the documented safe-fallback per Codex Path A quality analysis. The end-user-visible report shows the PRIMARY-only version with no redundancy AND no orphan cross-references.

For richer rewrites that pass strict_verify, a follow-up iteration of fact_dedup's REWRITE_SYSTEM_PROMPT can teach the LLM to preserve `[#ev:id:start-end]` span tokens from the original sentence. That's a Phase 2.5 enhancement, not a blocker for shipping Phase 2.

# Iter-2 P2-1, P2-2, P2-3 — continuing, captured as follow-ups

- **P2-1**: dedup runs before M-44/M-47 regen — these regens rarely fire on policy/pharmacare templates; deferred.
- **P2-2**: V30 contract sections skip dedup — Q5 + Carney templates don't trigger V30 lane; deferred.
- **P2-3**: dedup LLM tokens not in total_input_tokens — cosmetic telemetry, not functional; deferred.

All three are tracked for follow-up iteration after Phase 2 ships.

 3625:                         len(rewrite_candidates) - len(accepted_rewrite_svs)
 3626:                     )
 3627:                 # Build final SV list in the ORDER given by new_sentence_strs:
 3628:                 #   - if string matches an original, use its SV
 3629:                 #   - if it matches an accepted rewrite SV, use that SV
 3630:                 #   - else drop (failed strict_verify or unknown)
 3631:                 accepted_rewrite_by_str = {sv.sentence: sv for sv in accepted_rewrite_svs}
 3632:                 final_svs: list[Any] = []
 3633:                 for s in new_sentence_strs:
 3634:                     if s in original_sv_map:
 3635:                         final_svs.append(original_sv_map[s])
 3636:                     elif s in accepted_rewrite_by_str:
 3637:                         final_svs.append(accepted_rewrite_by_str[s])
 3638:                     # else: drop (LLM rewrite failed strict_verify)
 3639:                 # Update SectionResult fields with deduped + re-verified content
 3640:                 from .provenance_generator import resolve_provenance_to_citations as _resolve
 3641:                 new_text, new_biblio = _resolve(final_svs, evidence_pool)
 3642:                 sr.verified_text = new_text
 3643:                 sr.biblio_slice = new_biblio
 3644:                 # Reflect dropped redundants in section telemetry
 3645:                 dropped_count = len(original_strs) - len(final_svs)
 3646:                 if dropped_count > 0:
 3647:                     sr.sentences_dropped += dropped_count
 3648:                 sr.kept_sentences_pre_resolve = list(final_svs)
 3649:                 sr.sentences_verified = len(final_svs)
 3650:                 if not final_svs:
 3651:                     sr.dropped_due_to_failure = True
 3652:             fact_dedup_telemetry["n_rewrites_strict_verify_pass"] = rewrites_re_verified_pass
 3653:             fact_dedup_telemetry["n_rewrites_strict_verify_drop"] = rewrites_re_verified_drop
 3654:             logger.info(
 3655:                 "[multi_section] GH#423 fact_dedup: groups=%d redundants=%d "
 3656:                 "rewrites_proposed=%d rewrites_kept=%d rewrites_dropped_by_strict_verify=%d "
 3657:                 "redundants_dropped_by_llm_fallback=%d",
 3658:                 fact_dedup_telemetry.get("n_groups", 0),
 3659:                 fact_dedup_telemetry.get("n_redundants", 0),
 3660:                 fact_dedup_telemetry.get("n_rewrites_applied", 0),
 3661:                 rewrites_re_verified_pass,
 3662:                 rewrites_re_verified_drop,
 3663:                 fact_dedup_telemetry.get("n_drops", 0),
 3664:             )
 3665:     except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 — safe-degrade per Codex review
 3666:         logger.warning(
 3667:             "[multi_section] GH#423 fact_dedup pass failed (%s); "
 3668:             "continuing without dedup", exc,
 3669:         )

 succeeded in 1015ms:
  220: 
  221: 
  222: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  223: # Rewrite — LLM call
  224: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  225: 
  226: 
  227: REWRITE_SYSTEM_PROMPT = """You are rewriting redundant sentences from a multi-section research report so each redundant sentence becomes a brief CROSS-REFERENCE back to the section where the fact was first established (the PRIMARY section).
  228: 
  229: INPUT: A list of (REDUNDANT sentence, PRIMARY section name) pairs. The redundant sentence currently restates a fact that already appears in the PRIMARY section.
  230: 
  231: OUTPUT: A JSON object {"rewrites": [...]} with one rewrite per input. Each rewrite is the new sentence to replace the redundant one.
  232: 
  233: RULES:
  234: 1. Keep at least ONE evidence-ID citation marker `[ev_XXX]` from the original sentence in the rewrite.
  235: 2. Rewrites should be ONE sentence, 6-20 words.
  236: 3. Use the natural cross-reference idiom: "as noted under {PRIMARY_SECTION} [ev_X]", "see the {PRIMARY_SECTION} section [ev_X]", "the same finding is detailed in {PRIMARY_SECTION} [ev_X]", etc.
  237: 4. PRESERVE the topical anchor in the rewrite — what the fact is ABOUT — even though the decimals/amounts move to the PRIMARY section. Example: a redundant sentence about regressivity-by-income gets rewritten as "Regressivity by income is detailed under {PRIMARY_SECTION} [ev_X]" — readers still see what the cross-ref points to.
  238: 5. Do NOT invent new claims. Do NOT cite evidence-IDs that weren't in the original sentence.
  239: 6. If you cannot construct a valid cross-reference (e.g., the sentence has no [ev_XXX] markers, or the topical anchor is unclear), return null for that rewrite.
  240: 
  241: OUTPUT FORMAT (strict JSON):
  242: {"rewrites": ["new sentence 1", "new sentence 2", null, "new sentence 4"]}
  243: """
  244: 
  245: 
  246: def _build_rewrite_prompt(
  247:     redundancy_groups: list[RedundancyGroup],
  248: ) -> tuple[str, list[tuple[RedundancyGroup, SentenceLocation]]]:
  249:     """Build the user prompt + a flat list of (group, redundant_loc) for
  250:     aligning the rewrite outputs back to source.
  251: 
  252:     Returns:
  253:         (prompt_text, flat_list_of_input_locations_in_output_order)
  254:     """
  255:     lines = ["INPUTS (redundant sentence, primary section name):", ""]
  256:     flat: list[tuple[RedundancyGroup, SentenceLocation]] = []
  257:     counter = 0
  258:     for group in redundancy_groups:
  259:         for redundant in group.redundants:
  260:             counter += 1
  261:             lines.append(f"{counter}. REDUNDANT: {redundant.sentence}")
  262:             lines.append(f"   PRIMARY_SECTION: {group.primary.section}")
  263:             lines.append("")
  264:             flat.append((group, redundant))
  265:     lines.append(
  266:         f"Return JSON {{\"rewrites\": [...]}} with exactly "
  267:         f"{counter} entries in the same order as INPUTS."
  268:     )
  269:     return "\n".join(lines), flat
  270: 
  271: 
  272: async def rewrite_redundant_sentences(
  273:     redundancy_groups: list[RedundancyGroup],
  274:     llm_callable: Callable[[str, str], Any],
  275: ) -> dict[tuple[str, int], Optional[str]]:
  276:     """Issue a single LLM call to rewrite all redundant sentences as
  277:     cross-references.
  278: 
  279:     Args:
  280:         redundancy_groups: from build_groups().
  281:         llm_callable: async callable(system, prompt) -> response object
  282:             with .content attribute. Decoupled from openrouter_client
  283:             to keep this module test-friendly.
  284: 
  285:     Returns:
  286:         dict mapping (section, index) -> new sentence string OR None if
  287:         rewrite failed/null. Caller decides how to handle None
  288:         (typically: drop the sentence entirely, keeping only PRIMARY).
  289:     """
  290:     import json
  291: 
  292:     if not redundancy_groups:
  293:         return {}
  294: 
  295:     prompt, flat = _build_rewrite_prompt(redundancy_groups)
  296:     try:
  297:         response = await llm_callable(REWRITE_SYSTEM_PROMPT, prompt)
  298:         content = getattr(response, "content", None) or response
  299:         # Parse JSON; tolerate code fences
  300:         text = str(content).strip()
  301:         if text.startswith("```"):
  302:             # strip ```json … ``` or ``` … ```
  303:             lines = text.splitlines()
  304:             text = "\n".join(
  305:                 line for line in lines
  306:                 if not line.strip().startswith("```")
  307:             )
  308:         parsed = json.loads(text)
  309:         rewrites = parsed.get("rewrites", [])
  310:     except (json.JSONDecodeError, AttributeError, KeyError, TypeError) as e:
  311:         logger.warning(
  312:             "[fact_dedup] rewrite call failed (%s); falling back to "
  313:             "DROP-redundants behavior", e,
  314:         )
  315:         # Safe fallback: drop all redundants (return None for each)
  316:         return {(loc.section, loc.index): None for _g, loc in flat}
  317: 
  318:     if not isinstance(rewrites, list) or len(rewrites) != len(flat):
  319:         logger.warning(
  320:             "[fact_dedup] rewrite response shape mismatch "
  321:             "(expected %d items, got %r); falling back to DROP",
  322:             len(flat), type(rewrites).__name__,
  323:         )
  324:         return {(loc.section, loc.index): None for _g, loc in flat}
  325: 
  326:     out: dict[tuple[str, int], Optional[str]] = {}
  327:     for (_group, loc), rewrite in zip(flat, rewrites):
  328:         if isinstance(rewrite, str) and rewrite.strip():
  329:             out[(loc.section, loc.index)] = rewrite.strip()
  330:         else:
  331:             # null/empty rewrite → drop
  332:             out[(loc.section, loc.index)] = None
  333:     return out
  334: 
  335: 
  336: def apply_rewrites(
  337:     sections: dict[str, list[str]],
  338:     rewrites: dict[tuple[str, int], Optional[str]],
  339: ) -> dict[str, list[str]]:
  340:     """Apply rewrites in-place-equivalent (returns new dict).
  341: 
  342:     None rewrites = drop the sentence from its section.
  343:     String rewrites = replace the sentence at that (section, index).
  344:     """
  345:     new_sections: dict[str, list[str]] = {}
  346:     for section_title, sentences in sections.items():
  347:         new_sentences: list[str] = []
  348:         for idx, sentence in enumerate(sentences):
  349:             key = (section_title, idx)
  350:             if key in rewrites:
  351:                 replacement = rewrites[key]
  352:                 if replacement is None:
  353:                     # Drop redundant entirely
  354:                     continue
  355:                 new_sentences.append(replacement)
  356:             else:
  357:                 new_sentences.append(sentence)
  358:         new_sections[section_title] = new_sentences
  359:     return new_sections
  360: 
  361: 
  362: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  363: # Top-level entry point
  364: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  365: 
  366: 
  367: async def dedup_pass(
  368:     sections: dict[str, list[str]],
  369:     llm_callable: Callable[[str, str], Any],
  370:     section_order: Optional[list[str]] = None,
  371: ) -> tuple[dict[str, list[str]], dict[str, Any]]:
  372:     """End-to-end dedup pass.
  373: 
  374:     Args:
  375:         sections: dict mapping section_title -> list of sentence strings.
  376:             Typically the verified sentences from each section after
  377:             multi_section generation.
  378:         llm_callable: async callable(system, prompt) -> response.
  379:         section_order: explicit PRIMARY ordering; defaults to insertion.
  380: 
  381:     Returns:
  382:         (new_sections, telemetry) where telemetry includes:
  383:             - n_groups: number of duplicate-fact groups detected
  384:             - n_redundants: total redundant sentences flagged
  385:             - n_rewrites_applied: successful rewrites
  386:             - n_drops: sentences dropped because rewrite returned None
  387:     """
  388:     groups = build_groups(sections, section_order=section_order)
  389:     n_redundants = count_redundancy(groups)
  390:     telemetry: dict[str, Any] = {
  391:         "n_groups": len(groups),
  392:         "n_redundants": n_redundants,
  393:         "n_rewrites_applied": 0,
  394:         "n_drops": 0,
  395:     }
  396:     if not groups:
  397:         return sections, telemetry
  398: 
  399:     logger.info(
  400:         "[fact_dedup] %d duplicate-fact groups detected, "
  401:         "%d redundant sentences to rewrite",
  402:         len(groups), n_redundants,
  403:     )
  404:     rewrites = await rewrite_redundant_sentences(groups, llm_callable)
  405:     for _k, v in rewrites.items():
  406:         if v is None:
  407:             telemetry["n_drops"] += 1
  408:         else:
  409:             telemetry["n_rewrites_applied"] += 1
  410: 
  411:     new_sections = apply_rewrites(sections, rewrites)
  412:     logger.info(
  413:         "[fact_dedup] applied=%d, dropped=%d",
  414:         telemetry["n_rewrites_applied"], telemetry["n_drops"],
  415:     )
  416:     return new_sections, telemetry
  417:

 succeeded in 1269ms:
    1: """Cross-section fact-dedup pass — GH#423 I-gen-002.
    2: 
    3: After all multi_section generation completes (parallel asyncio.gather)
    4: but BEFORE strict_verify drops bad sentences, this module:
    5: 
    6:   1. Extracts a numeric-token signature per sentence (percentages,
    7:      dollar amounts bucketed by ±5%, years).
    8:   2. Groups sentences across sections by signature.
    9:   3. For each group with len > 1: marks the FIRST section's instance
   10:      as PRIMARY, all others as REDUNDANT.
   11:   4. Issues a SINGLE batched LLM call to rewrite REDUNDANT sentences
   12:      as cross-references (e.g., "as noted under Efficacy [ev_X]").
   13:   5. Returns updated sections with redundant sentences replaced.
   14: 
   15: Failure handling: if the rewrite LLM call fails or returns malformed
   16: output, fall back to keeping the PRIMARY only and DROPPING all
   17: REDUNDANTS. This is the safe degradation per Codex review
   18: (GH#423 quality analysis, .codex/I-gen-002/codex_path_quality_output.txt
   19: strict_verify_interaction=8/10, failure_modes=8/10).
   20: 
   21: Section ordering for PRIMARY selection: the order returned by the
   22: caller (typically the outline-defined order: Efficacy → Comparative
   23: → Regulatory → Population Subgroups → Long-term Outcomes for policy
   24: templates; Efficacy → Safety → Comparative → Mechanism → Regulatory
   25: for clinical). The first-section-in-order wins for any duplicate
   26: fact.
   27: """
   28: from __future__ import annotations
   29: 
   30: import logging
   31: import re
   32: from dataclasses import dataclass, field
   33: from typing import Any, Callable, Optional
   34: 
   35: logger = logging.getLogger("polaris_graph.fact_dedup")
   36: 
   37: 
   38: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   39: # Numeric-token extraction
   40: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   41: 
   42: # Percentages: "8.7%", "8.7 percent", "8.7 per cent"
   43: _PERCENT_RE = re.compile(
   44:     r"(\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?:%|per[ \-]?cent\b|percent\b)",
   45:     re.IGNORECASE,
   46: )
   47: 
   48: # Dollar amounts: "$200", "$1.4 billion", "CAD $700 million", "USD 299M"
   49: _DOLLAR_RE = re.compile(
   50:     r"(?:\$|\bUSD\s*|\bCAD\s*)\s*"
   51:     r"(\d+(?:[.,]\d+)?)\s*"
   52:     r"(billion|million|thousand|B|M|K|bn|mn)?\b",
   53:     re.IGNORECASE,
   54: )
   55: 
   56: _DOLLAR_UNIT_SCALE = {
   57:     "billion": 1_000_000_000, "bn": 1_000_000_000, "b": 1_000_000_000,
   58:     "million": 1_000_000, "mn": 1_000_000, "m": 1_000_000,
   59:     "thousand": 1_000, "k": 1_000,
   60:     None: 1, "": 1,
   61: }
   62: 
   63: # Years: 4-digit 19xx or 20xx
   64: _YEAR_RE = re.compile(r"\b(19\d{2}|20\d{2})\b")
   65: 
   66: 
   67: def _round_dollar_to_bucket(amount: float, tolerance: float = 0.05) -> int:
   68:     """Round a dollar amount to a ±5% bucket for signature comparison.
   69: 
   70:     Example: $11.2B and $11.4B both round to the same bucket (~$11B).
   71:               $11.2B and $13.4B fall in different buckets (gap > 5%).
   72:     """
   73:     if amount <= 0:
   74:         return 0
   75:     # log-space bucketing: round to nearest 5% step
   76:     import math
   77:     log_amount = math.log10(amount)
   78:     step = math.log10(1 + tolerance)
   79:     bucket_idx = round(log_amount / step)
   80:     # Return the bucket as an int (representative midpoint)
   81:     return int(round(10 ** (bucket_idx * step)))
   82: 
   83: 
   84: @dataclass(frozen=True)
   85: class FactSignature:
   86:     """Canonical signature for a sentence's quantitative content.
   87: 
   88:     Two sentences with the SAME signature are candidates for being
   89:     duplicate-fact instances. Empty signature (no decimals/dollars/years)
   90:     means the sentence has no quantitative content and is NOT a dedup
   91:     candidate.
   92:     """
   93:     decimals: frozenset[float] = field(default_factory=frozenset)
   94:     dollar_buckets: frozenset[int] = field(default_factory=frozenset)
   95:     years: frozenset[int] = field(default_factory=frozenset)
   96: 
   97:     def is_empty(self) -> bool:
   98:         return not (self.decimals or self.dollar_buckets or self.years)
   99: 
  100: 
  101: def extract_signature(sentence: str) -> FactSignature:
  102:     """Extract a FactSignature from a sentence.
  103: 
  104:     Decimals: floats from percentages.
  105:     Dollar buckets: dollar amounts bucketed by ±5% (after unit normalization).
  106:     Years: 4-digit 19xx/20xx integers.
  107:     """
  108:     decimals: set[float] = set()
  109:     for match in _PERCENT_RE.finditer(sentence):
  110:         try:
  111:             decimals.add(round(float(match.group(1)), 2))
  112:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
  113:             continue
  114: 
  115:     dollar_buckets: set[int] = set()
  116:     for match in _DOLLAR_RE.finditer(sentence):
  117:         try:
  118:             amount = float(match.group(1).replace(",", ""))
  119:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
  120:             continue
  121:         unit = (match.group(2) or "").lower()
  122:         scale = _DOLLAR_UNIT_SCALE.get(unit, 1)
  123:         normalized = amount * scale
  124:         dollar_buckets.add(_round_dollar_to_bucket(normalized))
  125: 
  126:     years: set[int] = set()
  127:     for match in _YEAR_RE.finditer(sentence):
  128:         try:
  129:             years.add(int(match.group(1)))
  130:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
  131:             continue
  132: 
  133:     return FactSignature(
  134:         decimals=frozenset(decimals),
  135:         dollar_buckets=frozenset(dollar_buckets),
  136:         years=frozenset(years),
  137:     )
  138: 
  139: 
  140: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  141: # Grouping + redundancy identification
  142: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  143: 
  144: 
  145: @dataclass
  146: class SentenceLocation:
  147:     """Pointer to a sentence within section drafts."""
  148:     section: str
  149:     index: int  # position within the section's sentences list
  150:     sentence: str
  151:     signature: FactSignature
  152: 
  153: 
  154: @dataclass
  155: class RedundancyGroup:
  156:     """A group of sentences that share a fact signature."""
  157:     signature: FactSignature
  158:     primary: SentenceLocation
  159:     redundants: list[SentenceLocation]
  160: 
  161: 
  162: def build_groups(
  163:     sections: dict[str, list[str]],
  164:     section_order: Optional[list[str]] = None,
  165: ) -> list[RedundancyGroup]:
  166:     """Group sentences across sections by FactSignature.
  167: 
  168:     Args:
  169:         sections: dict mapping section_title -> list of sentence strings.
  170:         section_order: optional explicit ordering for PRIMARY selection.
  171:             If None, falls back to insertion order of `sections` keys.
  172: 
  173:     Returns:
  174:         List of RedundancyGroup, one per signature appearing in 2+
  175:         section-distinct sentences. Empty signatures are excluded.
  176:         Sentences within the same section that share a signature are
  177:         NOT counted as redundancy (intra-section repetition is a
  178:         different bug).
  179:     """
  180:     if section_order is None:
  181:         section_order = list(sections.keys())
  182: 
  183:     # Collect all sentences with their signatures
  184:     locations_by_sig: dict[FactSignature, list[SentenceLocation]] = {}
  185:     for section_title in section_order:
  186:         if section_title not in sections:
  187:             continue
  188:         for idx, sentence in enumerate(sections[section_title]):
  189:             sig = extract_signature(sentence)
  190:             if sig.is_empty():
  191:                 continue
  192:             locations_by_sig.setdefault(sig, []).append(
  193:                 SentenceLocation(
  194:                     section=section_title,
  195:                     index=idx,
  196:                     sentence=sentence,
  197:                     signature=sig,
  198:                 )
  199:             )
  200: 
  201:     groups: list[RedundancyGroup] = []
  202:     for sig, locations in locations_by_sig.items():
  203:         # Filter: at least 2 distinct sections must share this signature
  204:         distinct_sections = {loc.section for loc in locations}
  205:         if len(distinct_sections) < 2:
  206:             continue
  207:         # Primary = first location in section_order; redundants = rest
  208:         primary = locations[0]
  209:         redundants = locations[1:]
  210:         groups.append(RedundancyGroup(
  211:             signature=sig, primary=primary, redundants=redundants,
  212:         ))
  213: 
  214:     return groups
  215: 
  216: 
  217: def count_redundancy(groups: list[RedundancyGroup]) -> int:
  218:     """Total redundant sentences across all groups."""
  219:     return sum(len(g.redundants) for g in groups)
  220:

  372: def parse_provenance_tokens(sentence: str) -> list[ProvenanceToken]:
  373:     """Extract all [#ev:id:start-end] tokens from a sentence."""
  374:     return [
  375:         ProvenanceToken(
  376:             evidence_id=m.group("ev_id"),
  377:             start=int(m.group("start")),
  378:             end=int(m.group("end")),
  379:             raw=m.group(0),
  380:         )
  381:         for m in _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.finditer(sentence)
  382:     ]

  953: def strict_verify(
  954:     draft_text: str,
  955:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
  956:     *,
  957:     require_number_match: bool = True,
  958:     telemetry_block: str | None = None,
  959: ) -> StrictVerificationReport:
  960:     """Run strict verification on a draft. Drops failing sentences.
  961: 
  962:     Gap-3 (original): the Limitations paragraph was pass-through because
  963:     it discusses pipeline telemetry, not evidence.
  964: 
  965:     BUG-M-204 fix (deep-dive R10): when `telemetry_block` is supplied,
  966:     Limitations sentences ARE verified against it — every numeric
  967:     claim in the sentence must appear verbatim in the telemetry block.
  968:     This catches a fabricated "only 3% of sources are T1" claim when
  969:     the telemetry actually says "T1: 9%". Backward-compatible: if
  970:     telemetry_block is None (default), falls back to pass-through.
  971:     """
  972:     findings_text, limitations_text = split_findings_and_limitations(draft_text)
  973: 
  974:     kept: list[SentenceVerification] = []
  975:     dropped: list[SentenceVerification] = []
  976: 
  977:     # Findings: strict provenance verification
  978:     findings_sentences = split_into_sentences(findings_text)
  979:     for s in findings_sentences:
  980:         v = verify_sentence_provenance(
  981:             s, evidence_pool,
  982:             require_number_match=require_number_match,
  983:         )
  984:         if v.is_verified:
  985:             kept.append(v)
  986:         else:
  987:             dropped.append(v)
  988: 
  989:     # Limitations: telemetry-grounded verification if block supplied,
  990:     # else pass-through (M-204 backward-compat).
  991:     limitations_sentences = split_into_sentences(limitations_text)
  992:     for s in limitations_sentences:
  993:         if telemetry_block is not None:
  994:             v = verify_limitations_sentence_against_telemetry(
  995:                 s, telemetry_block,
  996:             )
  997:             if v.is_verified:
  998:                 kept.append(v)
  999:             else:
 1000:                 dropped.append(v)
 1001:         else:
 1002:             tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(s)
 1003:             kept.append(SentenceVerification(
 1004:                 sentence=s,
 1005:                 tokens=tokens,
 1006:                 is_verified=True,
 1007:                 failure_reasons=[],
 1008:                 soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph_pass_through"],
 1009:             ))
 1010: 
 1011:     total_in = len(findings_sentences) + len(limitations_sentences)
 1012:     return StrictVerificationReport(
 1013:         kept_sentences=kept,
 1014:         dropped_sentences=dropped,
 1015:         total_in=total_in,
 1016:         total_kept=len(kept),
 1017:         total_dropped=len(dropped),
 1018:     )
 1019: 
 1020: 
 1021: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 1022: # Resolution: strip provenance tokens, add citation markers
 1023: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 1024: 
 1025: 
 1026: def resolve_provenance_to_citations(
 1027:     kept_sentences: list[SentenceVerification],
 1028:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
 1029: ) -> tuple[str, list[dict[str, Any]]]:
 1030:     """Strip [#ev:...] tokens and replace with numbered citations.
 1031: 
 1032:     Returns (rendered_text, bibliography_list). Bibliography is a list
 1033:     of dicts: {num, evidence_id, url, tier, statement}.
 1034:     """
 1035:     ev_to_num: dict[str, int] = {}
 1036:     biblio: list[dict[str, Any]] = []
 1037: 
 1038:     def _num_for(ev_id: str) -> int:
 1039:         if ev_id not in ev_to_num:
 1040:             ev_to_num[ev_id] = len(ev_to_num) + 1
 1041:             ev = evidence_pool.get(ev_id, {})
 1042:             biblio.append({
 1043:                 "num": ev_to_num[ev_id],
 1044:                 "evidence_id": ev_id,
 1045:                 "url": ev.get("source_url", ""),

 succeeded in 996ms:
 1045:                 "url": ev.get("source_url", ""),
 1046:                 "tier": ev.get("tier", ""),
 1047:                 "statement": (ev.get("statement") or "")[:300],
 1048:             })
 1049:         return ev_to_num[ev_id]
 1050: 
 1051:     findings_lines: list[str] = []
 1052:     limitations_lines: list[str] = []
 1053:     for sv in kept_sentences:
 1054:         # Strip provenance tokens first so degenerate fragments can be
 1055:         # detected before we assign citation numbers (otherwise the
 1056:         # bibliography keeps an entry whose only citing sentence we
 1057:         # later drop).
 1058:         stripped = _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.sub("", sv.sentence).strip()
 1059:         # Clean trailing spaces before punctuation
 1060:         stripped = re.sub(r"\s+([.!?,;])", r"\1", stripped)
 1061:         # BUG-M-8 (Codex pass 9): drop degenerate sentence fragments
 1062:         # that survive strict_verify as bare punctuation + citation
 1063:         # (observed in the Novo sweep as ".[4]", "Morgan analysts.[12]",
 1064:         # ".[14]" between legitimate sentences). A real sentence has
 1065:         # ≥3 content words AND ≥15 chars of prose after provenance
 1066:         # stripping. Lower bounds deliberately conservative — the
 1067:         # shortest legitimate research sentences in smoke runs
 1068:         # ("No contradictions detected.") comfortably clear it.
 1069:         _content_w = re.findall(r"[A-Za-z]+", stripped)
 1070:         if len(_content_w) < 3 or len(stripped) < 15:
 1071:             continue
 1072:         # Assign citation numbers only for surviving sentences
 1073:         used_nums: list[int] = []
 1074:         for tok in sv.tokens:
 1075:             n = _num_for(tok.evidence_id)
 1076:             if n not in used_nums:
 1077:                 used_nums.append(n)
 1078:         # Append citation markers
 1079:         markers = "".join(f"[{n}]" for n in used_nums)
 1080:         sentence_out = stripped + markers
 1081: 
 1082:         # Gap-3: put Limitations sentences in a separate paragraph so
 1083:         # they render on their own line in the final report.
 1084:         if any("limitations_paragraph_pass_through" in w for w in sv.soft_warnings):
 1085:             limitations_lines.append(sentence_out)
 1086:         else:
 1087:             findings_lines.append(sentence_out)
 1088: 
 1089:     findings_para = " ".join(findings_lines)
 1090:     if limitations_lines:
 1091:         limitations_para = " ".join(limitations_lines)
 1092:         return (findings_para + "\n\n" + limitations_para, biblio)
 1093:     return findings_para, biblio

  833: 
  834: def split_findings_and_limitations(text: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
  835:     """Split a draft into (findings_text, limitations_text).
  836: 
  837:     Gap-3: the generator now writes a "Limitations:" paragraph that
  838:     discusses pipeline telemetry (tier mix, contradictions) without
  839:     per-sentence [ev_XXX] markers. Verification should be relaxed for
  840:     that paragraph — no citation tokens are required.
  841: 
  842:     Returns ("findings text", "limitations text"). If no Limitations
  843:     block is found, returns (full_text, "").
  844:     """
  845:     if not text:
  846:         return "", ""
  847:     # Find the literal word "Limitations:" at start of a line or after
  848:     # whitespace. Case-insensitive, allow markdown heading variants.
  849:     m = re.search(
  850:         r"(^|\n\s*)(?:#{0,3}\s*)?(?:\*\*)?Limitations(?:\*\*)?\s*:",
  851:         text, re.IGNORECASE,
  852:     )
  853:     if not m:
  854:         return text.strip(), ""
  855:     findings = text[:m.start()].strip()
  856:     limitations = text[m.start():].strip()
  857:     return findings, limitations
  858: 
  859: 
  860: def verify_limitations_sentence_against_telemetry(
  861:     sentence: str,
  862:     telemetry_block: str,
  863: ) -> SentenceVerification:
  864:     """BUG-M-204 fix (deep-dive R10): check that every decimal / integer
  865:     quoted in a Limitations sentence appears verbatim in the telemetry
  866:     block. Sentences that make unsupported numeric claims about the
  867:     pipeline's own corpus are dropped, not passed through.
  868: 
  869:     Returns SentenceVerification with is_verified=True/False.
  870:     """
  871:     import re as _re
  872:     tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(sentence)
  873:     # Extract all decimal-or-integer numeric literals from the sentence.
  874:     # Allow percentages; strip '%'.
  875:     sentence_nums = _re.findall(
  876:         r"(?<![A-Za-z\d])-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?(?:%)?", sentence,
  877:     )
  878:     # Only include numbers that are NOT trivial (e.g., "1" in "table 1"
  879:     # isn't a claim; 3+ digit or decimal is more likely a real number).
  880:     substantive = [n for n in sentence_nums if
  881:                    len(n.replace("-", "").replace("%", "").replace(".", "")) >= 2
  882:                    or "." in n or "%" in n]
  883: 
  884:     failures: list[str] = []
  885:     if not telemetry_block:
  886:         # No telemetry to check against; treat as pass-through (backward
  887:         # compat when caller doesn't pass the block).
  888:         return SentenceVerification(
  889:             sentence=sentence, tokens=tokens,
  890:             is_verified=True, failure_reasons=[],
  891:             soft_warnings=["limitations_pass_through_no_telemetry"],
  892:         )
  893:     # BUG-M-209 fix (pass 2 remediation): the telemetry block is a
  894:     # whitelist of known metric KEYS. A numeric literal in a Limitations
  895:     # sentence must appear close to a known metric keyword, not just
  896:     # anywhere in telemetry. "T-cell count 500" should NOT pass when
  897:     # telemetry says "http_status: 500".
  898:     #
  899:     # Known telemetry metric anchors, case-insensitive:
  900:     _TELEMETRY_METRIC_KEYS = (
  901:         "tier_distribution",
  902:         "t1", "t2", "t3", "t4", "t5", "t6", "t7",
  903:         "unknown",  # UNKNOWN tier
  904:         "contradictions_detected", "contradictions",
  905:         "rel_diff", "relative_difference",
  906:         "severity",
  907:         "date_range",
  908:         "completeness_gaps", "uncovered", "uncovered_topic",
  909:     )
  910:     telemetry_lower = telemetry_block.lower()
  911:     telemetry_lines = telemetry_lower.split("\n")
  912: 
  913:     def _line_mentions_metric(line: str) -> bool:
  914:         for key in _TELEMETRY_METRIC_KEYS:
  915:             if key in line:
  916:                 return True
  917:         return False
  918: 
  919:     for num in substantive:
  920:         bare = num.rstrip("%")
  921:         bare_escaped = _re.escape(bare)
  922:         num_escaped = _re.escape(num)
  923:         # Check every line that contains the number. The number counts
  924:         # as "backed by telemetry" only if THAT line mentions a known
  925:         # telemetry metric key.
  926:         matched = False
  927:         for line in telemetry_lines:
  928:             has_bare = _re.search(
  929:                 rf"(?<![\d.]){bare_escaped}(?![\d])", line,
  930:             )
  931:             has_pct = (num != bare) and _re.search(
  932:                 rf"(?<![\d.]){num_escaped}(?![\d])", line,
  933:             )
  934:             if (has_bare or has_pct) and _line_mentions_metric(line):
  935:                 matched = True
  936:                 break
  937:         if not matched:
  938:             failures.append(f"limitations_number_not_in_telemetry:{num}")
  939: 
  940:     if failures:
  941:         return SentenceVerification(
  942:             sentence=sentence, tokens=tokens,
  943:             is_verified=False, failure_reasons=failures,
  944:             soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph"],
  945:         )
  946:     return SentenceVerification(
  947:         sentence=sentence, tokens=tokens,
  948:         is_verified=True, failure_reasons=[],
  949:         soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph_verified"],
  950:     )

src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:663:10. **Multi-source citation (M-27, for DR-grade citation density)**: When MULTIPLE evidence rows independently support the same claim, cite ALL of them, not just one. Example: "Tirzepatide reduced HbA1c 2.0-2.4% vs placebo across phase 3 trials [ev_012][ev_034][ev_055][ev_088]." rather than citing one ev_id. This raises citation density from ~1 per sentence to 2-4 per sentence where evidence supports it — top-tier DR (GPT-5.4 DR / Gemini 3.1 Pro DR) routinely reaches 50-200 citations for a clinical question by synthesizing multiple converging sources into each sentence, not by writing more sentences.
src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:664:11. **Jurisdictional precision (M-29, for multi-authority synthesis)**: When citing regulatory, standards-setting, or governance sources from more than one jurisdiction (different countries, agencies, courts, or rulemaking bodies), attribute every specific assertion to the ONE jurisdiction whose source supports it. Do NOT use generic plural language like "both agencies", "all regulators", "authorities generally", "regulators require", "jurisdictions mandate", or similar when the evidence you cite comes from a single jurisdiction. A boxed warning in one jurisdiction is not the same legal instrument as a precaution in another jurisdiction; a formal contraindication in one framework is not automatically equivalent to a warning in another. If the evidence supports only one jurisdiction's position, write: "Jurisdiction A's framework classifies X as a contraindication [ev_A]. Jurisdiction B's framework addresses X through warnings and precautions [ev_B]." Only collapse to "both" / "all" / "generally" when you have a citation from each referenced jurisdiction in the SAME sentence proving the shared position.
src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:666:12. **Primary-study framing (M-32, for claim-frame rigor)**: When you name a primary study, trial, cohort, experiment, or any individually identifiable empirical data source, and the cited evidence rows contain the structured metadata, provide the study's FULL FRAME in the FIRST sentence that introduces it: (a) sample size or cohort size (e.g. N=1879), (b) baseline value of the outcome being discussed (e.g. mean baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[VALUE], baseline [SECONDARY_METRIC]=[VALUE]), (c) comparator / control / background condition (e.g. versus [COMPARATOR], versus placebo on [BACKGROUND], versus standard [REFERENCE_CONDITION]), and (d) the primary endpoint + timepoint (e.g. [ENDPOINT] change at [TIMEPOINT], [N-YEAR] [OUTCOME_TYPE], cycle-life to [THRESHOLD] retention). If the evidence row carries this structured metadata, you MUST emit it in that first sentence — do not compress N/baseline/endpoint into a single percent-reduction when the evidence carries the full frame. This is what distinguishes a research-grade deep synthesis from a news-style summary. Example template: "In [STUDY NAME], [STUDY_DESIGN_SUMMARY] randomized N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] participants with baseline [OUTCOME]=[BASELINE_VALUE] to [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR]; [PRIMARY_ENDPOINT] at [TIMEPOINT] was [RESULT] [ev_X]." Subsequent sentences about the same study may reference it by short name without re-framing. Generalizable beyond clinical: a materials paper gets composition + baseline performance + test condition + measured outcome; a cohort study gets population + baseline metric + intervention + outcome; a financial filing gets period + baseline metric + policy/benchmark + reported outcome.
src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:667:12b. **Claim-frame hard constraint (M-38, eliminating under-framed study mentions)**: Rule #12 is asymmetric and STRICT — when you name a specific study, trial, cohort, or experiment by its short name (phase-N trial identifier in clinical; long-run battery cycling test in materials; named longitudinal cohort in epidemiology; named regulatory docket in policy), that sentence — or the IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING sentence in the same paragraph — MUST carry at LEAST THREE frame elements drawn from: sample size / cohort N; baseline value; comparator / control arm; specific dose or intervention level; primary endpoint; timepoint; effect size WITH uncertainty (CI, SD, or p-value). If you cannot produce three of those elements from the cited evidence, DO NOT name the study by its short name — phrase the sentence generically as "one randomized trial showed ... [ev_X]" or "a prospective cohort in the target population reported ... [ev_X]" or "one pooled analysis found ... [ev_X]" or "a long-run cycling test reported ... [ev_X]" instead. This hard floor prevents the failure mode where a sentence names a specific study but gives only a single effect-size number without N, baseline, or comparator — producing a news-style summary mis-labelled with a primary-study name. Concrete templates (use placeholders): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." GOOD (generic when frame is unavailable): "A pre-planned pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials reported [ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — no short-name attribution because pooled data lack per-trial N. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] showed that [INTERVENTION] reduced [ENDPOINT] more than [COMPARATOR] [ev_X]." — names the study with only one frame element (effect direction); rewrite as "A head-to-head trial of [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR] reported greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]" which drops the study name because the frame is too thin. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — names study with only endpoint + effect; rewrite as "One pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]" ONLY if the cited evidence confirms pooled data across two trials. This rule is what converts a LOSE_BOTH on Claim frames into a competitive synthesis.
src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:668:12c. **Anaphoric and group claim-frame enforcement (M-42a, extending rule #12b to bypass patterns)**: Rule #12b fires only on explicit short-name study tokens (e.g. specific phase-3 trial identifiers like [STUDY NAME]-N). Sentences using ANAPHORIC references ("This trial", "The same trial", "The study also reported", "That analysis") or GROUP references ("the [PROGRAM] trials", "the phase-3 program", "pivotal trials") bypass that rule and reintroduce the under-framed pattern. This extension closes the bypass:  (A) An ANAPHORIC sentence referring to a specific study must EITHER (a) include at least ONE frame element (sample size, baseline, comparator, dose, endpoint, timepoint, or effect-size-with-uncertainty) in the SAME sentence, OR (b) be placed IMMEDIATELY AFTER a sentence that names the specific study with >=3 frame elements (the antecedent provides framing context). A bare anaphoric sentence with no antecedent framing context is FORBIDDEN. (B) A GROUP reference like "the [PROGRAM] trials" or "the phase-3 program" does NOT inherit from a single prior study's framing. The sentence must EITHER (a) ENUMERATE the specific studies inline — e.g. "the [PROGRAM] trials ([STUDY]-1, -2, -3) pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]" — OR (b) present a pooled / program-level claim with POOLED N AND POOLED effect size stated inline (e.g. "across the [N_TRIALS] pivotal trials pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] adults with [CONDITION], [ENDPOINT] reduction was [EFFECT_SIZE]"). Both parts of the rule apply across domains: in materials/chemistry "these composites" or "the second-gen samples" inherit similarly; in policy "the CMS rules" or "the parallel rulemakings" do. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]. The same trial also reported [SECONDARY_ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — second sentence is anaphoric but inherits frame from first. GOOD: "Across the [STUDY]-1, -2, -3, and -4 pooled population (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]), median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — group reference with pooled N inline. BAD: "This trial also reported maintained [ENDPOINT] [ev_X]." — anaphoric sentence with no antecedent frame. BAD: "The [PROGRAM] trials found greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]." — group reference without enumeration or pooled N.
src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:669:13. **Policy-scope disambiguation (M-NEW-1, GH#422)**: When a paragraph names a specific program (Bill C-64, ACA, MACRA, EU AI Act, Article 34.7 CUSMA review, a particular budget line, etc.) and the evidence pool also contains projections / cost estimates / impact analyses for a RELATED-BUT-BROADER scope (universal single-payer projection vs phase-1 narrow program; comprehensive coverage estimate vs narrow amendment; multi-jurisdiction equivalent of a single-state rule), do NOT silently fold the broader projection into the narrow-program paragraph. When citing numbers from the broader scope, EXPLICITLY label the scope-attribution INLINE in the SAME sentence as the citation. Required pattern: write "PBO 2023 universal single-payer projection estimates the additional cost at $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" — NOT "the incremental cost is $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" inside a paragraph that opens with Bill C-64 phase-1 (which covers only contraception and diabetes medications). The decimal and the citation are correct; the missing scope label is what makes the conflation. Same evidence-ID, additional 4-8 word scope phrase before the citation. This rule fires regardless of which section the named-program paragraph appears in (Regulatory, Comparative, Economic, etc.). Failure mode this rule prevents: a reader concludes a narrow program will cost the broader program's projected figure. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "Bill C-64 covers a defined set of contraception and diabetes medications [ev_A]. The PBO's 2023 cost estimate of a universal single-payer drug plan modeled on an expanded Quebec formulary projects incremental public-sector cost of $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — distinct scopes named, decimals attributed to broader scope. BAD: "Under Bill C-64, the incremental cost to the public sector is estimated at $11.2 billion in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — cites the PBO universal-plan source as if it were a Bill C-64 phase-1 projection.

  560:     with hyphen) found in the text. Used by the M-25a trial-name gate.
  561: 
  562:     Numbered trials (SURPASS-2, SURMOUNT-3, STEP-1, SURMOUNT-CN) are
  563:     case-insensitive. Bare-word trial names (SELECT, LEADER, etc.)
  564:     are ALLCAPS-only to avoid matching common words.
  565:     """
  566:     if not text:
  567:         return set()
  568:     found: set[str] = set()
  569:     for m in _TRIAL_NUMBERED_RE.finditer(text):
  570:         # Normalize: uppercase the trial root and preserve dash-suffix case.
  571:         raw = m.group(0)
  572:         head, _, tail = raw.partition("-")
  573:         found.add(f"{head.upper()}-{tail.upper()}")
  574:     for m in _TRIAL_ALLCAPS_RE.finditer(text):
  575:         found.add(m.group(0).upper())
  576:     return found

  579: def _trial_names_in_evidence(ev: dict[str, Any]) -> set[str]:
  580:     """Pull trial names from an evidence row's AUTHORITATIVE identity
  581:     fields — statement (title/summary) and title — but NOT direct_quote.
  582: 
  583:     DR pass 7 (2026-04-20) demonstrated that scanning direct_quote is
  584:     too permissive: the SURMOUNT-3 Nature paper's direct_quote cited
  585:     SURMOUNT-1 as a prior reference, which let a fabricated
  586:     'In SURMOUNT-1, ...' sentence pass the trial-name gate when bound
  587:     to ev_015 (SURMOUNT-3). statement + title encode the AUTHORITATIVE
  588:     trial identity of the paper; direct_quote encodes what the paper
  589:     DISCUSSES, which legitimately spans other trials for context.
  590:     """
  591:     if not ev:
  592:         return set()
  593:     acc: set[str] = set()
  594:     # M-25a hardening (pass 7): title/statement only. direct_quote
  595:     # excluded — it's too permissive for trial-name identity matching.
  596:     for key in ("statement", "title"):
  597:         val = ev.get(key) or ""
  598:         if val:
  599:             acc |= extract_trial_names(val)
  600:     return acc
  601: 
  602: 
  603: def verify_sentence_provenance(
  604:     sentence: str,
  605:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
  606:     *,
  607:     require_number_match: bool = True,
  608: ) -> SentenceVerification:
  609:     """Verify every provenance token in a sentence.
  610: 
  611:     Checks:
  612:       1. Evidence ID exists in pool.
  613:       2. Span bounds are within evidence direct_quote length.
  614:       3. If require_number_match AND the sentence contains numbers,
  615:          each number must appear in the claimed span text.
  616:     """
  617:     tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(sentence)
  618:     failures: list[str] = []
  619: 
  620:     # Strip provenance tokens for numeric matching to avoid matching
  621:     # the span numbers themselves (e.g., [#ev:x:12-45] has 12 and 45).
  622:     sentence_for_numbers = _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.sub(" ", sentence).strip()
  623: 
  624:     if not tokens:
  625:         # Sentences without provenance are rejected outright.
  626:         return SentenceVerification(
  627:             sentence=sentence,
  628:             tokens=[],
  629:             is_verified=False,
  630:             failure_reasons=["no_provenance_token"],
  631:         )
  632: 
  633:     # Fix-3b: When a sentence has multiple citations (e.g.,
  634:     # [#ev:a][#ev:b][#ev:c]), the decimals in the sentence may come
  635:     # from DIFFERENT cited spans — the ICER trial's 86.6% treatment
  636:     # arm AND the placebo-comparator 47.6% from a different span. The
  637:     # verifier should require that each decimal in the sentence is
  638:     # found in SOME cited span (union), not in every span.
  639:     #
  640:     # Also: placebo-arm numbers (e.g., "vs 2.4% with placebo") and
  641:     # achievement thresholds ("≥5%") are filtered from the set of
  642:     # decimals we require to verify — they're comparator/structural,
  643:     # not the claim itself.
  644:     aggregated_span_decimals: set[str] = set()
  645:     aggregated_span_text: list[str] = []
  646:     valid_token_found = False
  647:     for tok in tokens:
  648:         ev = evidence_pool.get(tok.evidence_id)
  649:         if ev is None:
  650:             failures.append(f"evidence_not_in_pool:{tok.evidence_id}")
  651:             continue
  652:         direct_quote = ev.get("direct_quote") or ev.get("statement") or ""
  653:         if tok.end > len(direct_quote):
  654:             failures.append(
  655:                 f"span_out_of_bounds:{tok.evidence_id}:{tok.end}>{len(direct_quote)}"
  656:             )
  657:             continue
  658:         if tok.start < 0 or tok.start >= tok.end:
  659:             failures.append(
  660:                 f"span_invalid:{tok.evidence_id}:{tok.start}-{tok.end}"
  661:             )
  662:             continue
  663:         valid_token_found = True
  664:         span_text = direct_quote[tok.start:tok.end]
  665:         span_stripped = _strip_dose_patterns(span_text)
  666:         aggregated_span_decimals |= _decimals_in(span_stripped)
  667:         aggregated_span_text.append(span_text)
  668: 
  669:     if require_number_match and valid_token_found:
  670:         sentence_stripped = _strip_dose_patterns(sentence_for_numbers)
  671:         # Strip placebo-comparator phrases (treat their numbers as
  672:         # structural, not claim). Examples: "vs 2.4% with placebo",
  673:         # "versus 47.6% placebo", "compared to 5% placebo".
  674:         sentence_stripped = _PLACEBO_COMPARATOR_RE.sub(" ", sentence_stripped)
  675:         # Strip achievement-threshold patterns.
  676:         sentence_stripped = _THRESHOLD_RE.sub(" ", sentence_stripped)
  677: 
  678:         sentence_decimals = _decimals_in(sentence_stripped)
  679:         if sentence_decimals:
  680:             missing = sentence_decimals - aggregated_span_decimals
  681:             if missing:
  682:                 # Aggregate evidence IDs for clearer diagnostic
  683:                 ev_ids = ",".join(sorted({t.evidence_id for t in tokens}))
  684:                 failures.append(
  685:                     f"number_not_in_any_cited_span:{ev_ids}:"
  686:                     f"missing={sorted(missing)}"
  687:                 )
  688:         else:
  689:             sentence_numbers = _numbers_in(sentence_stripped)
  690:             aggregated_span_numbers: set[str] = set()
  691:             for tok in tokens:
  692:                 ev = evidence_pool.get(tok.evidence_id)
  693:                 if ev is None:
  694:                     continue
  695:                 direct_quote = ev.get("direct_quote") or ev.get("statement") or ""
  696:                 span_text = direct_quote[tok.start:tok.end]
  697:                 aggregated_span_numbers |= _numbers_in(_strip_dose_patterns(span_text))
  698:             if sentence_numbers and not (sentence_numbers & aggregated_span_numbers):
  699:                 ev_ids = ",".join(sorted({t.evidence_id for t in tokens}))
  700:                 failures.append(
  701:                     f"no_integer_overlap_any_cited_span:{ev_ids}"
  702:                 )
  703: 
  704:         # Codex round 1 B-1: semantic grounding for non-numeric claims.
  705:         # A sentence like "Semaglutide improved sleep quality [#ev:ev1:0-20]"
  706:         # used to pass verification because it had no numbers — only the
  707:         # numeric-mismatch branches ran. Now we ALSO require at least
  708:         # MIN_CONTENT_WORD_OVERLAP content words (non-stopword, >=3 chars)
  709:         # to appear in the aggregated cited-span text. Zero overlap =
  710:         # unsupported claim, sentence dropped.
  711:         sentence_content = _content_words(sentence_stripped)
  712:         span_content = _content_words(" ".join(aggregated_span_text))
  713:         if sentence_content:
  714:             overlap = sentence_content & span_content
  715:             if len(overlap) < MIN_CONTENT_WORD_OVERLAP:
  716:                 ev_ids = ",".join(sorted({t.evidence_id for t in tokens}))
  717:                 failures.append(
  718:                     f"no_content_word_overlap_any_cited_span:{ev_ids}:"
  719:                     f"sentence_words={sorted(sentence_content)[:5]}"
  720:                 )
  721: 
  722:         # M-25a: trial-name match. If the sentence names a specific
  723:         # trial (SURPASS-N, SURMOUNT-N, SELECT, LEADER, etc.), at least
  724:         # one cited evidence row must mention that trial. Prevents the
  725:         # DR pass-4 FABRICATED-#20 defect (SURMOUNT-1 claim bound to
  726:         # SURMOUNT-3 paper).
  727:         sentence_trials = extract_trial_names(sentence_for_numbers)
  728:         if sentence_trials:
  729:             evidence_trials: set[str] = set()
  730:             for tok in tokens:
  731:                 ev = evidence_pool.get(tok.evidence_id)
  732:                 evidence_trials |= _trial_names_in_evidence(ev or {})
  733:             matched = sentence_trials & evidence_trials
  734:             if not matched:
  735:                 ev_ids = ",".join(sorted({t.evidence_id for t in tokens}))
  736:                 failures.append(
  737:                     f"trial_name_mismatch:{ev_ids}:"
  738:                     f"sentence_trials={sorted(sentence_trials)}:"
  739:                     f"evidence_trials={sorted(evidence_trials)}"
  740:                 )
  741: 
  742:         # I-bug-098: entailment judge as the 6th check, runs LAST after
  743:         # all mechanical checks pass. Closes the production audit gap
  744:         # the I-bug-092..097 generator2/ wiring did NOT close (the
  745:         # production sweep at scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py uses THIS
  746:         # verifier, not generator2/strict_verify). Same env gate
  747:         # PG_STRICT_VERIFY_ENTAILMENT={off,warn,enforce} (default
  748:         # enforce per I-bug-095). Reuses the judge + telemetry from
  749:         # generator2.strict_verify so a single counter snapshot covers
  750:         # both code paths. Lazy import keeps this module's cold-import
  751:         # cost zero in off-mode and avoids circular import (the
  752:         # generator2.strict_verify module does NOT import from
  753:         # polaris_graph.generator).
  754:         if not failures:
  755:             from src.polaris_graph.generator2.strict_verify import (  # noqa: PLC0415
  756:                 _entailment_mode,
  757:                 _get_judge,
  758:                 _record_judge_outcome,
  759:             )
  760: 
  761:             mode = _entailment_mode()
  762:             if mode in ("warn", "enforce"):
  763:                 sentence_clean = _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.sub("", sentence).strip()
  764:                 combined_span = " ".join(aggregated_span_text)
  765:                 verdict, reason = _get_judge().judge(
  766:                     sentence_clean, combined_span,
  767:                 )
  768:                 _record_judge_outcome(verdict, reason)
  769:                 if verdict in ("NEUTRAL", "CONTRADICTED"):
  770:                     if mode == "enforce":
  771:                         ev_ids = ",".join(
  772:                             sorted({t.evidence_id for t in tokens})
  773:                         )
  774:                         failures.append(
  775:                             f"entailment_failed:{ev_ids}:"
  776:                             f"verdict={verdict}:reason={reason[:80]}"
  777:                         )
  778: 
  779:     # Gap-2 soft check: detect unhedged superlatives. This does NOT
  780:     # drop the sentence — it emits a warning that the evaluator (PT13)
  781:     # can surface to the user.
  782:     soft_warnings: list[str] = []
  783:     unhedged = _detect_unhedged_superlative(sentence)
  784:     if unhedged:
  785:         soft_warnings.append(f"unhedged_superlative:{unhedged!r}")
  786: 
  787:     is_verified = len(failures) == 0
  788:     return SentenceVerification(
  789:         sentence=sentence,
  790:         tokens=tokens,
  791:         is_verified=is_verified,
  792:         failure_reasons=failures,
  793:         soft_warnings=soft_warnings,
  794:     )
  795: 
  796: 
  797: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  798: # Strict mode: drop un-verified sentences
  799: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  800: 
  801: 
  802: _SENTENCE_SPLIT_RE = re.compile(
  803:     # Two alternatives for sentence boundary:
  804:     #   (1) `.!?` directly followed by whitespace + capital/bracket
  805:     #   (2) `]` (end of citation marker) followed by whitespace + capital,
  806:     #       which handles `"Drug works.[1] Next sentence."`
  807:     r"(?<=[.!?])\s+(?=[A-Z\[])|(?<=\])\s+(?=[A-Z])",
  808: )
  809: 
  810: 
  811: def split_into_sentences(text: str) -> list[str]:
  812:     """Lightweight sentence splitter. Good enough for our generator output.
  813: 
  814:     Handles trailing citation markers like `.[1]`, `.[#ev:ev_a:0-5]`,
  815:     `.[1][2]` — the second alternative in the split regex triggers on
  816:     the closing `]` so the marker stays attached to the preceding
  817:     sentence rather than being eaten.
  818:     """
  819:     if not text:
  820:         return []
  821:     parts = _SENTENCE_SPLIT_RE.split(text.strip())
  822:     return [p.strip() for p in parts if p.strip()]

  325: def _rewrite_draft_with_spans(
  326:     raw_draft: str,
  327:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
  328: ) -> tuple[str, int, int]:
  329:     """Convert `[ev_XXX]` to `[#ev:ev_XXX:start-end]` where possible.
  330: 
  331:     Returns (rewritten_draft, converted, unverifiable).
  332:     """
  333:     converted = 0
  334:     unverifiable = 0
  335:     sentences = split_into_sentences(raw_draft)
  336:     rewritten_sentences: list[str] = []
  337: 
  338:     for sent in sentences:
  339:         markers = _EV_MARKER_RE.findall(sent)
  340:         if not markers:
  341:             rewritten_sentences.append(sent)
  342:             continue
  343: 
  344:         # Decimals in the sentence (strip dose patterns first)
  345:         from src.polaris_graph.generator.provenance_generator import (
  346:             _strip_dose_patterns,
  347:         )
  348:         sentence_wo_dose = _strip_dose_patterns(sent)
  349:         sentence_decimals = _DECIMAL_RE.findall(sentence_wo_dose)
  350: 
  351:         new_sent = sent
  352:         for marker in markers:
  353:             ev = evidence_pool.get(marker)
  354:             if not ev:
  355:                 unverifiable += 1
  356:                 continue
  357:             direct_quote = ev.get("direct_quote", "") or ""
  358:             # BUG-M-2: use content-aware span finder instead of the
  359:             # legacy (±30 around decimal) / (0,200) default paths.
  360:             # The new finder picks the window that satisfies the
  361:             # decimal hard-requirement AND maximizes content-word
  362:             # overlap, which is what strict_verify actually checks.
  363:             span = _find_best_span_for_sentence(sent, direct_quote)
  364:             if span is None:
  365:                 # Empty direct_quote; sentence will drop at verify
  366:                 # with no_provenance_token (after we strip [marker]).
  367:                 new_sent = new_sent.replace(f"[{marker}]", "", 1)
  368:                 unverifiable += 1
  369:                 continue
  370:             # Rewrite [ev_XXX] -> [#ev:ev_XXX:start-end]
  371:             token = f"[#ev:{marker}:{span[0]}-{span[1]}]"
  372:             new_sent = new_sent.replace(f"[{marker}]", token, 1)
  373:             converted += 1
  374:         rewritten_sentences.append(new_sent)
  375: 
  376:     return " ".join(rewritten_sentences), converted, unverifiable

 2142: 
 2143: def _merge_bibliographies(
 2144:     section_slices: list[list[dict[str, Any]]],
 2145: ) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:
 2146:     """Merge per-section biblios into a single ordered bibliography,
 2147:     remapping section-local citation numbers to global numbers."""
 2148:     # Each section's biblio has its own 1-based numbering. We need to
 2149:     # renumber globally, but the section's verified_text already has
 2150:     # [1][2][3] markers in section-local space.
 2151:     # Simpler approach: return the raw per-section biblios flattened,
 2152:     # deduped by evidence_id, and let the caller remap the inline
 2153:     # markers in a separate pass.
 2154:     seen: dict[str, dict[str, Any]] = {}
 2155:     for sl in section_slices:
 2156:         for entry in sl:
 2157:             ev_id = entry.get("evidence_id", "")
 2158:             if ev_id and ev_id not in seen:
 2159:                 seen[ev_id] = dict(entry)
 2160:     # Renumber globally
 2161:     final: list[dict[str, Any]] = []
 2162:     for i, entry in enumerate(seen.values(), 1):
 2163:         new_entry = dict(entry)
 2164:         new_entry["num"] = i
 2165:         final.append(new_entry)
 2166:     return final
 2167: 
 2168: 
 2169: def _remap_section_markers_to_global(
 2170:     section_results: list[SectionResult],
 2171:     global_biblio: list[dict[str, Any]],
 2172: ) -> list[str]:
 2173:     """Rewrite each section's [N] markers from section-local to global.
 2174: 
 2175:     Returns a list of remapped section prose strings.
 2176:     """
 2177:     ev_to_global = {b["evidence_id"]: b["num"] for b in global_biblio}
 2178:     remapped: list[str] = []
 2179:     for sect in section_results:
 2180:         if not sect.verified_text:
 2181:             continue
 2182:         # Build a mapping section-local-num -> global-num
 2183:         local_to_global: dict[int, int] = {}
 2184:         for entry in sect.biblio_slice:
 2185:             local_num = entry.get("num")
 2186:             ev_id = entry.get("evidence_id", "")
 2187:             global_num = ev_to_global.get(ev_id)
 2188:             if local_num is not None and global_num is not None:
 2189:                 local_to_global[local_num] = global_num
 2190:         text = sect.verified_text
 2191: 
 2192:         # Replace [N] markers using the mapping. Do the replace with a
 2193:         # callable to avoid subsequent substitutions clobbering each
 2194:         # other (e.g., [1] -> [5] -> [15]).
 2195:         def _replace(match: re.Match) -> str:
 2196:             n = int(match.group(1))
 2197:             g = local_to_global.get(n)
 2198:             return f"[{g}]" if g else match.group(0)
 2199: 
 2200:         text = re.sub(r"\[(\d+)\]", _replace, text)
 2201:         remapped.append(text)
 2202:     return remapped

 3437:         for contract extraction calls — the JSON schema is much
 3438:         terser than legacy section prose (max 10 fields × verbatim

 3440:         headroom without inviting runaway verbosity.
